Current Commentary

The Misfortune of the Hong Kong-Guangdong Banking System 19

— Yan

The head office of the Hong Kong Guangdong Bank declared suspension of payments on the 4th of this month due to a run on the bank by overseas Chinese depositors. The bank was unable to meet the withdrawal demands. This affected the bank's branches in Guangzhou, Shanghai, Hankou, and San Francisco, which subsequently suspended operations. Other Chinese commercial banks in Hong Kong were also affected by the run. The Hong Kong National Commercial Savings Bank implemented a restriction on withdrawals, limiting depositors in the savings section to one-fifth of their deposits every ten days. Only now has the run gradually subsided. After this crisis occurred, the Ministry of Finance immediately ordered the banking associations in Shanghai and Hankou to take over the assets of the Guangdong Bank branches in those locations. However, the issue of how to manage the aftermath remains to be planned.

The decline in the Guangdong Bank's operations has been going on for some time. Reading the bank's business reports makes this evident. In terms of liabilities, the public reserve fund item was still listed at 1.1 million yuan at the end of the 21st year. By the end of the 22nd year, this item no longer existed. As for the deposit item, it was over 31.6 million yuan at the end of the 20th year, but decreased to over 25.4 million yuan the following year. It further decreased to over 21.6 million yuan the year before last, and then to over 16.2 million yuan last year. This is a sharp decrease of about one-half compared to four years ago. In terms of assets, the cash on hand was over 11.8 million yuan at the end of the 20th year, but decreased to over 8.3 million yuan the following year. It further decreased to over 7.1 million yuan the year before last, and then to only over 2.1 million yuan last year. This is a sharp decrease of more than three-quarters compared to four years ago. The amount deposited with counterpart banks in other locations was over 10.7 million yuan at the end of the 20th year, but only over 3.1 million yuan remained last year. This is a decrease of about 70 percent. The loan item was over 16.4 million yuan at the end of the 20th year, over 15.6 million yuan the following year, over 13.7 million yuan the year before last, and then over 12.7 million yuan last year. This is a decrease of only one-fifth over four years. The total receipts and payments were over 49.5 million yuan at the end of the 20th year, decreased to over 41.1 million yuan the following year, further decreased to over 32.1 million yuan the year before last, and then decreased to over 26.7 million yuan last year. This is a decrease of about 47 percent over four years. From the disappearance of the public reserve fund, it can be asserted that the bank suffered considerable losses several years ago. It is likely that the entire public reserve fund was used to offset the losses. The sharp decrease in the various asset items is clearly due to the outflow of deposits. In addition, it is worth noting the weakening and stagnation of loans. This phenomenon proves that the bank's loans are frozen and difficult to recover.

The Guangdong Bank and the Hong Kong National Bank are both registered with the Hong Kong government and use the Hong Kong dollar as their base currency. Their internal organization, accounting system, and business strategies differ slightly from other Chinese commercial banks. These so-called Hong Kong-Guangdong banking systems have their own distinct banking system and have historically had special influence in the Guangdong business community. However, there have been many bankruptcies over the past decade. Early examples include the Gongshang and Huashang banks, and more recently, the Wuhua (Shanghai branch) and Jiahua banks. The Guangdong Bank, which was known for its long history and strong capital in the system, has now declared suspension of operations under the guise of reorganization. This can truly be said to be a misfortune for the Hong Kong-Guangdong financial community. This is probably a manifestation of the economic decline of Hong Kong and Guangdong. However, part of the reason still lies in the unsound organization and management techniques of the banks in this system. It is not too late to mend the fold after a sheep has been lost. From now on, Hong Kong and Guangdong bankers should know how to remedy the situation.

The League of Nations Considers Imposing a Disguised Protectorate on Abyssinia, Five-Nation Committee Currently Considering 20

(London) According to a report in the Daily Telegraph, the five-nation committee of the League of Nations Council, which is dealing with the Italian-Abyssinian problem, is currently considering implementing a protectorate system for Abyssinia, with Abyssinia becoming a protectorate of Italy. The method is similar to the treaty signed between Britain and Iraq in 1930. However, the concern is that the Emperor of Abyssinia may not be willing to sign such a treaty, and may not even be able to sign such a treaty. The Daily Telegraph further stated that Britain cannot accept any proposals that seek to resolve the current crisis by allowing Italy to maintain a military occupation of Abyssinia. (Havas News Agency, Eighth Dispatch)

(Paris) The newspapers on Sunday unanimously discussed the development of the Italian-Abyssinian case in vivid language, but were pessimistic about the future of the matter. They believed that the five-nation committee may not be better than the three-nation conference in Paris. The Geneva correspondent of the Volfr newspaper stated that most delegations in Geneva also hold this view. Mussolini's policy is to delay the agenda, wait for the disintegration of the Council, and then take the opportunity to attack Abyssinia. If the League of Nations encounters an attack on Abyssinia, it will take sanctions and gain the support of most governments. At this time, if Italy still insists on fighting, Britain will send troops to occupy the western part of Abyssinia, thereby protecting its interests. Sir Eden has hinted that the British fleet is prepared to respond to the situation, which has caused a deep impression. According to a certain source in Geneva, this demonstration will force Italy to return to the League of Nations. If sanctions are put into practice, it will show the world that no country, if it insists on its own way and is unwilling to listen to the wishes of other countries, can escape the sanctions stipulated in the entire League of Nations treaty. After the Italian-Abyssinian war reports are released, it can be predicted that world opinion will favor sanctions. Bodinna, a diplomatic reporter for the Paris Echo, also stated that world opinion does not approve of Italy's actions. Britain's military preparations, both at sea and on land, are precise and may be far greater than those prepared to be announced. (National News Agency, Ninth Dispatch)

The 16th League of Nations Assembly Opens: Reviewing Achievements of the Past Year, Encountering the Italian-Abyssinian Case Again, Proving that International Issues are Inseparable 21

(Geneva) The 16th Annual Assembly of the League of Nations opened at 10:55 this morning. Chairman Qi Naga of Argentina, who is also the chairman of the Council, delivered the opening speech. He first stated Argentina's efforts in the past to maintain peace, especially its efforts to mediate the Grand Chaco dispute. He then briefly described the activities of the League of Nations over the past year, such as proposing to send international troops to the Saar region to maintain order during the plebiscite to determine whether it should belong to France or Germany, and achieving a peaceful solution. Later, when King Alexander of Yugoslavia visited France, he was assassinated in Marseille. At that time, the international situation was extremely tense, but peace was maintained thanks to the efforts of the League of Nations. Today, the League of Nations is once again discussing a difficult dispute, namely the Italian-Abyssinian problem. "In short, the progress of the League of Nations may be delayed, and the past discussions of international disputes by the League of Nations may be forgotten, but it has been proven since the past fifteen years that all international issues are interconnected and inseparable, and that international issues must be discussed openly based on justice and honor. The past secret diplomacy is no longer applicable and must be replaced by open diplomacy. These are the gains since the establishment of the League of Nations. The Congress has become the basic organization for safeguarding good relations between nations. If this mission can be adhered to, then even if the international situation is sometimes dim, the League of Nations will be able to overcome all difficulties and regain light."

After Chairman Qi Naga finished his speech, the Assembly extended the meeting by one hour. When the meeting resumed, it immediately began to elect the chairman. As a result, Czech Foreign Minister Pi Yishi was elected with 54 votes against 49 votes. Yesterday, it was expected that after Yang Xiao was elected, Qi Naga would congratulate Pi Yishi, and Pi Yishi took office as chairman amidst applause from representatives of various countries. He also made slight revisions to the agenda of the Assembly, and removed the issue of the embargo on arms exports to various countries, "and included the Grand Chaco dispute and the draft convention on the suppression of political prisoners on the agenda. The Assembly adjourned at 1:11 p.m., and the next meeting was scheduled to continue at 5:30 p.m. (Havas, Ninth Dispatch)

(Geneva) Czech Foreign Minister Pi Yishi was re-elected as the official chairman. Pi stepped onto the podium amidst cheers from the crowd and declared in a brief speech, "I believe that we will be able to find a new path to peace, eliminate difficulties, and emerge victorious." Italian Representative Arosic and British Foreign Secretary Hall were among the first to arrive at the meeting. (Reuters, Ninth Dispatch)

Italian Ambassador Sends Overtures to Germany, Presents Credentials Three Weeks Early 22

(Berlin) Italian Ambassador to Germany, Adolies, was originally scheduled to present his credentials in three weeks. The German government, at the request of the Italian government, held the ceremony for presenting the credentials to German leader Hitler yesterday. This shows that Italy is now urgently seeking friendship with Germany. This matter was initially kept secret and was only announced last night. The Italian ambassador was received by Hitler and Foreign Minister Nulte with ordinary military honors. Presenting credentials to the German leader on Sunday is something that has not happened for many years. The Italian ambassador delivered a sincere speech, expressing his hope that the two countries would cooperate in friendship and mutually benefit. In his reply, Hitler stated that fascism and National Socialism shared the same goals. At Hitler's invitation, the Italian ambassador will travel to Nuremberg today to attend the annual congress of the National Socialist Party. Apart from the Italian ambassador, only the Polish representative is attending this congress. (Reuters, Ninth Dispatch)

(Berlin) The new Italian Ambassador to Germany, Adorigo, paid a visit to Hitler this morning to present the German leader with his letter of credence and the letter of recall of the former Ambassador, Serpenti. Mr. Ado issued a statement to Hitler in which he stated: "From what I feel, Europe and the countries of the world are now experiencing an important period in history and that the relations between Italy and Germany are particularly important to peace and international equilibrium. Italy is proceeding with a vast undertaking aimed at rendering more firm her power and prestige. Italy now requests that all countries understand her legitimate interests, just as she understands the legitimate interests of all other countries". In his reply, Mr. Hitler stated: "Italy and Germany's relationship is critical to the future political development and effective peaceful cooperation among all countries. I share the same sentiment with you on this issue. Further, I believe that justice and mutual understanding are necessary for the existence of all peoples. Only once that is understood can cooperation between countries be discussed. The ideals that Fascist Italy and National Socialist Germany embrace are largely identical, and therefore the relationship between the two countries will surely become more and more smooth, benefitting all countries of the world. This is what I deeply value". (Havas Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

(Berlin) A well-known humorous weekly in Munich was confiscated by the police today for publishing a satirical drawing about the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, depicting Death wielding a scythe in a field and shouting, "Only I am the big winner in East Africa!" The attitude of the German authorities is that Germany intends to be friendly with the major powers and has nothing to do with the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, so it does not want to hurt the feelings of the Italians. (Reuters, Ninth Dispatch)

British Foreign Secretary Arrives in Geneva, Cooperating with France to Prevent War, Laval Arrives Early for Meeting 23

(Geneva) British Foreign Secretary Hall arrived here this afternoon from London and will attend the League of Nations General Assembly opening tomorrow as the chief British delegate. The Foreign Secretary carried a letter to Eden informing him that Prime Minister Baldwin and other cabinet members fully support the policy he has taken in the Abyssinia case. When the Foreign Secretary passed through Paris, he made a short stop, telling reporters: "I am willing to cooperate with Laval and do my best to seek peace." Before departing from the United Kingdom, he had a meeting with Baldwin in Aix. Baldwin will return to London at the beginning of this week and has warned all cabinet members to be prepared to attend emergency meetings at any time. If necessary, he will convene them. (Reuters Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

(Paris) Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval was originally scheduled to go to Geneva on Tuesday morning. According to sources, he will now leave for Geneva on Monday evening in order to meet with British Foreign Secretary Hall in Geneva as soon as possible. (Havas Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

British-Italian Naval Exercises Attract Attention Throughout Europe 24

(Paris) The large-scale naval exercises conducted by the British Navy in the Mediterranean have attracted great attention throughout Europe, even though the British Navy Department has repeatedly stated that this is purely routine. Thirty-four British warships and the hospital ship Maine are currently docked at the main port of Alexandria in Egypt. Another fourteen warships arrived in Navarino, Greece, today. The British Royal Air Force in Alexandria is also very active, with an aircraft patrolling the skies day and night over the port and the area near the Apoke Arsenal, which is 13 miles northeast of Alexandria. At the same time, it is said that barbed wire defenses have been densely deployed around Malta. (Zilin News Agency Special Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

Syria, Hafa - Nine British destroyers arrived here today to replace the original seven. As for where these seven are now headed, no one knows. (Reuters Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch) Large-scale naval maneuvers will begin on the 17th of this month.

(London) More than 60 warships are concentrated in Portland and Weymouth in preparation for participation in the exercises. According to a report in the Daily Telegraph, the fuel and food carried by these warships are sufficient for two months of navigation, so that they can continue to sail thousands of miles if necessary without needing to replenish fuel in the middle of the voyage. (Havas Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

(Rome) A fleet of Italian submarines, totaling 70 submarines, a detachment of light cruisers, and part of the naval air force are conducting joint exercises between Sicily and the African coast. The conduct of these exercises is being kept secret and is expected to be completed by mid-September. The responsible parties here firmly deny that this move is directed against Britain. (Reuters Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

(Berlin) German warships are currently conducting exercises in the North Sea. This is the first time since the signing of the London Naval Treaty. Warships sailed to Heligoland all night yesterday and gathered there early this morning. The Baltic Sea Fleet has passed through the Kiel Canal and joined the North Sea Fleet for joint exercises. (Reuters Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

Abyssinian Government Announces that Italian Troops are Preparing to Attack 25

Abyssinian Capital - The Abyssinian government recently issued a communiqué stating: "According to reports from the northern provinces, a large number of troops are being mobilized along the border of Italian Eritrea. An Italian military invasion of Abyssinian territory appears imminent." (Havas Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

(Rome) Mussolini addressed a crowd of 70,000 from the balcony of the Palazzo Venezia today. As he was about to conclude, Mussolini asked, "Who will Abyssinia belong to?" The crowd shouted, "To Italy, to Italy!" Mussolini smiled broadly upon hearing this and appeared very happy. He then retreated into the palace, but the crowd outside continued to cheer. Mussolini then came out to the balcony again and asked if they wanted to meet for a moment longer. The crowd all shouted "Yes, yes!" After Mussolini retreated into the palace again, the welcomers continued to cheer for a considerable time before finally dispersing. (National News Agency Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital - Italian troops were heavily defeated by Abyssinian troops at Apokwa in 1896. If Italy goes to war with Abyssinia this time, its primary goal will be to avenge this previous defeat. It is said that the Italian army will first attack from the north. General Bono will lead a large army from Aduwa to Aksum. Abyssinian leader Siymum has 35,000 soldiers stationed there. Siymum seems to intend to resist for some time, allowing the Italian army to penetrate deeply. It is said that the Italian side has 100,000 white soldiers and thousands of local soldiers gathered in Eritrea. Their front line is very long, and the flanks are at risk of being harassed by Abyssinian guerrillas. It is said that the Abyssinian side has 50,000 well-equipped soldiers stationed in Gondar. In the south, General Graziani seems to be leading a crowd of 100,000 soldiers, advancing cautiously. However, the Italian soldiers are suffering greatly from the heat, and many are sick. Therefore, before the actual attack, it seems that reinforcements are still needed to help. The strategy of the Abyssinian army in the south is still undecided. It is likely that the main resistance will be staged before the important town of Harar. (Reuters Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital - The Italian government has decided to withdraw consulates from various locations. Foreigners in the Abyssinian capital believe that this is not a good omen, and they feel even more uneasy as the Italian embassy continues to prepare to return home. The Abyssinian Emperor guarantees the safety of Italian embassy and consular staff and prohibits all anti-Italian demonstrations. Official circles here did not express alarm after hearing the news of the withdrawal of the Italian consulates, believing that most of the consular staff carried equipment such as radio stations and engaged in espionage work. Among the Italian consuls who returned home last week was Consul Heibblamaco Falgoni of Kafa Province. Mr. Fa was injured in a hunting accident recently and was not fully recovered when he returned home. (National News Agency Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

Abyssinian Capital - Due to the serious situation, the Italian Embassy in Abyssinia has been specially authorized to advise Italian expatriates scattered in the interior of Abyssinia to concentrate in the Abyssinian capital to prevent accidents. However, the Italian clerics in the Kafa province will temporarily reside in the province, pending further orders. (Havas Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

(Rome) The Bank of Italy has recently raised the discount rate from 4.5% to 5%. (Havas Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

Prospects Dim for Another Stresa Conference: Doubts in Geneva 26

(Geneva) News reports from Rome state that Mussolini is willing to hold another conference in Stresa to discuss a solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. People in Geneva are quite skeptical about this. No formal proposal of this nature has yet been received. However, as the League of Nations' special five-member committee is currently dealing with the issue, a Stresa conference seems unlikely to materialize. Moreover, the previous Paris conference ended in failure, and the lessons learned from that event serve as a warning. The special five-member committee will meet today in a more difficult atmosphere than last week. While the committee is holding closed-door meetings, the League of Nations General Assembly is likely to discuss the Italian-Abyssinian dispute openly. There is a general hope that the Assembly will not issue any radical statements that would create new obstacles for the committee. (Reuters Dispatch, Ninth Dispatch)

(Geneva) The five-member committee of the League of Nations, which is handling the Italian-Abyssinian problem, has encountered conflicts of interest, which has hampered Britain's determination to make new recommendations to Italy. British representative Eden had urged the committee to submit a compromise plan to the League of Nations Council by September 14. Sources in London also stated that the British Cabinet fully supports Eden. Eden's attitude is becoming increasingly firm. However, Eden still faces several difficult problems that may prevent him from achieving his goals: (1) France is deeply concerned that excessive haste will jeopardize the newly harmonious French-Italian relations if a compromise cannot be reached, and French representative Laval expects Italy to reject any proposals for concessions. (2) Spain, while always adhering to strict moral principles, must also take into account its interests in Africa and the Mediterranean. However, Spanish representative Madariaga will likely focus on moral aspects and support Britain. (3) Turkey, like Soviet Russia, believes that the proposals of Britain and France are quite suspicious. However, Turkey and Italy also have a rivalry for dominance in the Balkans and the Mediterranean. (4) Poland, while always loyal to the League of Nations, is also showing a hesitant attitude. Italian representative Alosi has publicly stated that Poland is the most friendly member of the committee. The League of Nations General Assembly will open on Monday, and all peace efforts will proceed in unison. It is said that representatives of several small countries have decided to use the full force of the Assembly to prevent war. However, Irish Free State representative President Fan Lela has lost hope of becoming the chairman of the Assembly after announcing that he would fight to the end for this cause. It is likely that Czech representative Pixuan Shi will be elected as chairman at that time. (National News Agency Dispatch, Eighth Dispatch)

British Labour Party Leader Lansbury Advocates Church Mediation to Avert War, Disapproves of League of Nations Using Force 27

(London) Labour Party leader Lansbury, in an interview with a Reuters correspondent today, indicated that he might resign as leader of the Labour Party because he disagrees with the party's stance on the League of Nations' handling of the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. Lansbury stated that under no circumstances could he support the use of force, even by the League of Nations. He and his colleagues would prefer that the Labour Party elect another leader. Lansbury is currently organizing church leaders to strongly advise Mussolini on the necessity of peace. (8th, Reuters Dispatch)

Oil Rights Broker Runs Out of Gasoline En Route to Cairo 28

Cairo: Rickert, who handled the negotiations for the 75-year Ethiopian oil concession contract, ran out of gasoline today while driving from Suez to Cairo, about thirty miles from Cairo, and was unable to proceed. An interviewer from the Paris Concorde Daily witnessed this and inquired about the oil concession. Rickert replied that the Ethiopian oil and mining rights issue was very simple, but he doesn't understand how it became such a complex matter. He has received telegrams regarding new methods, but no decision has been made yet. When Rickert arrived in Suez earlier, he declined to comment and refused to answer reporters' questions, but said that the Ethiopian oil and mining rights he successfully negotiated would eventually start construction. He also said that he would arrive in London around September 15, at which time he could make a very detailed statement. (8th Reuters)

German Catholic Congress: Harmony Between Christian Doctrine and Germanism Will Lead to German Prosperity 29

(Berlin) Twenty thousand Catholics in Berlin held a congress today at the sports field. The newly appointed Catholic Bishop of Berlin, Moses, delivered a speech, stating: "The moral laws of Catholicism do not change with the trends of the times or racialism. If Christian doctrine and Germanism can be in harmony with each other, then the German people will surely become prosperous and strong." Subsequently, Vice-Bishop Steinmann spoke, saying: "We solemnly swear to fulfill our obligations to the nation, but right and wrong must be clearly distinguished, and we must never mistake falsehood for truth." (8th Havas News Agency)

German National Socialist Party Opens National Congress Today; Hitler Favors Diplomatic Representatives 30

Nuremberg: The National Socialist Party will open its national congress here at the city hall at 7:30 PM tomorrow, but the formal meeting will begin on Wednesday. The proceedings will be broadcast on the radio throughout the country. Before the arrival of the leaders this afternoon, the cornerstone laying ceremony will be held for Dutzendteich's new convention hall. The National Socialist Party's congress will be extended to Saturday. During this period, Hitler Youth will make a declaration, and the National Socialist Party will have various demonstrations and public declarations to determine the activities and goals of the National Socialist Party for the coming year. (9th National Lamp)

Baton Rouge: Senator Huey Long, a Democrat who is referred to as the "dictator of Louisiana," was suddenly attacked here and seriously injured. At the time, Long was on his way to the Louisiana House of Representatives to attend an extraordinary session because several bills that would increase Long's dictatorial power were to be introduced for discussion at today's meeting. Long was attending the meeting to try to ensure that these bills would pass, but as he walked along the passage connecting the State Senate and House of Representatives, someone suddenly pulled out a gun and shot him, hitting Long in the abdomen, causing heavy bleeding. He was immediately taken to a nearby hospital, and it is said that the injuries are quite serious. After the assailant fired the shot, Long's guards immediately arrested him. The assailant is a young man named Dr. Weiss, 30 years old, and is the son-in-law of State Judge Bowie. Rumors of a plot to assassinate Long have been circulating for some time. Long himself mentioned the matter in the Washington Senate, saying that several people had conspired to harm him in a hotel in New Orleans. This was overheard by Long's brother, who secretly used a radio in the next room to record the entire conspiracy on a recording. At the time, someone was heard saying, "Killing Long only requires one person, one gun, and one bullet. I'm prepared to draw lots to get this job." It was also heard that the mayor of New Orleans, Walmsley, was aware of the matter. However, Long did not care after learning of this plot. When other senators inquired about it, Long just smiled and said, "These things are like insuring my longevity, what is there to fear?" Unexpectedly, there was actually an assassination attempt today. However, whether this assassination is the result of the aforementioned conspiracy cannot be verified at this time. American Senator Long

Baton Rouge: Louisiana's uncrowned emperor, Senator Huey Long, was shot last night in the state capitol by the son-in-law of a political enemy. Fortunately, only one shot was fired, and the weapon malfunctioned, so he was spared a fatal wound. After Long was shot, blood spurted from his mouth, and he was immediately rushed to the hospital for emergency treatment. The assassin was Dr. Weiss, 30 years old, an ear, nose and throat doctor. After firing the shot, he was immediately killed by Long's guards with a submachine gun. Weiss was struck by forty bullets and died instantly. After Long was admitted to the hospital, the doctors determined that he had lost too much blood and could not be saved without a blood transfusion. More than a hundred people volunteered to donate blood. The doctors then tested their blood and selected several people. While Long was receiving the blood transfusion, he was delirious, but an hour later, he was able to talk to the doctors. This morning, the hospital issued a statement saying that Long's condition was satisfactory. The State legislature only convened at night to pass several of the bills sponsored by Long. Long has been one of the most colorful figures in American history for many years. He used all his strength to destroy the power of the opposition party to control the Louisiana legislature. As a result, the Louisiana legislature was reduced to an organization that only followed Long's orders. Long has eloquence and sweeps through thousands of men, able to cater to the psychology of the masses and gain their support. Long's theory of "sharing the wealth" made many people fantasize about future prosperity. Long regarded President Roosevelt as a formidable opponent, so he often spoke out against him. He recently stated that if Roosevelt or Hoover were nominated again next year, he would organize a third party and compete for the presidency. Long's unconventional behavior is known throughout the world. Once, when the captain of a German warship paid a formal visit, Long greeted him in casual clothes, causing an international diplomatic joke. Long is currently 42 years old. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

Baton Rouge: Senator Huey Long was attacked today in the Louisiana legislature, and it is reported that his injuries are very serious. Long's abdomen has been pierced, and his large intestine has been injured in two places. Doctors fear that Long may develop peritonitis. At the same time, blood is constantly flowing from Long's wound, so the chances of recovery are difficult to predict at this time. Everything will depend on the outcome of the blood transfusion therapy. Long received blood transfusion therapy shortly after being admitted to the hospital. The blood donor was a friend of Long's. Later news said that Long's condition was slightly better. (8th National Electric)

Baton Rouge: Senator Huey Long, the political dictator of Louisiana, has begun an attack on the federal government over the state government's powers. He convened the state legislature, held a special session, and introduced 31 bills. One of them would prohibit federal agents from exercising powers outside the Constitution in the state, with violators subject to a fine of 1,500 and imprisonment for one year. Another bill would allow the state government to sue the central government when the rights of the state government are taken away. Some observers believe that Long's actions are the biggest challenge to the federal government since the American Civil War. Long said today that he may ask the Supreme Court to rule on whether to ban New Deal personnel from working in Louisiana, and said that the federal government should not oversee elections in Louisiana. Canada and the United States Negotiate Reciprocal Trade Agreement; Exchange of Documents in Progress 33

Ottawa: The exchange of documents between the Canadian Minister to the United States and the U.S. government regarding the negotiation of a reciprocal trade agreement between the two countries. Canada proposes to apply its intermediate tariff rates to U.S. goods, so that the tariffs currently paid on more than 700 kinds of U.S. goods can be reduced, and other tariff reductions in Canada's trade agreements with other countries can also be applied to the United States. At the same time, in return, the United States should reduce the current import tariffs on Canadian fish, yams, milk, livestock, and certain agricultural and mineral products by half. These negotiations are currently in progress. (8th Reuters Dispatch)

However, in fact, the U.S. silver mining industry is insignificant, and even the number of hairpin workers is greater than the number of silver miners. Brackenridge severely rebuked the representatives of a very small number of western states for wasting national money and creating opportunities for speculators. Gold and Silver

British Gold: The price of gold in London today was 141 shillings and 2 pence, up half a penny.

British Silver: The London silver market fell by 0.0625 due to sales from China and India. Both spot and futures prices were 29 pence and 1.875. American purchases kept the market stable at the close.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet today. The opening price of the British-American exchange rate was 4 dollars and 92 and 4375 cents, lower by 4 and 75 cents compared to the closing price for U.S.-British purchases on Saturday. Within the first hour, it rebounded by 275, reaching 4 dollars and 92 and 8125 cents. The price fell by 125 at noon, but after two hours, it returned to 4 dollars and 92 and 8125 cents.

British-French: The opening price was 74 francs and 75, the same as the closing price on Saturday. At eleven o'clock, it rose by 4 points, reaching 74 francs and 79, with no further changes.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened sluggish this morning, as operators awaited the government report to be released at noon. The market lacked excitement, and price fluctuations were very small. The opening price rose by 5 points, then rose by another 3 points. Later, due to hedging sales, the price fell slightly.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market had very little trading. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 5.70, down 1 point.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to be stable at noon. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 5 shillings, 11 pence, and 75, up 1 penny and 1275.

American Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was good, but the Chicago wheat market opened with a gain of only 125. Later, due to profit-taking, prices plummeted. At the time of the dispatch, the price was half a point lower than the opening price. News of rain in the Southwest caused the market price to continue to fall by half a point. Later, due to some buying, the price rebounded by 25, but the number of gains was lost again due to continued hedging sales.

Rubber

New York: The New York rubber market opened with better sentiment, causing the price to rise by 3 points, because the London prices had improved. Trading was very sluggish before 10:20. Cheng Yun Visits President Wang to Inquire About Procedures for Entering Tibet 38

(Nanjing) Cheng Yun, the special envoy escorting the Panchen Lama back to Tibet, along with Luo Youren, director of the Panchen Lama's office, visited President Wang at the Executive Yuan at 10:00 AM on the 7th to inquire about the procedures for returning to Tibet and the funds for the journey. Cheng Yun must wait until the funds are in place and the procedures are completed before heading north to Qinghai to meet the Panchen Lama. (9th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Cheng Yun said that the Panchen Lama's return to Tibet has been in the works for a long time, but it has not been realized due to various reasons, and the journey is long and will take a lot of time. After a long period of preparation, the Tibetan affairs are now largely in order, and it is hoped that we can depart from Qinghai on the 15th of next month. The planned route is through Qinghai, Yushu, Xikang, and the border into Tibet. Most of the areas along the way are mountains and ridges, and the climate is cold. Not only are there few inhabitants, but there are even places where no vegetation grows. There are also several places where you can eat meat but not drink soup, and drink soup but not eat meat. Although the locals say that this is superstition, it is due to the special climate, which inevitably causes serious meat diseases. Also, there is a type of grass called "Deceitful Horse Grass" that grows everywhere in slightly warmer areas. If a horse eats it, it will die immediately, which is also a fact. Therefore, not only should people prepare sufficient food for this trip, but also horse feed to maintain the horses until we reach Tibet. We will use tents for accommodation along the way. If the weather is good and there is not much snow, we should be able to reach Tibet by the end of this year. I was ordered to escort the Panchen Lama back to Tibet, but I have limited talent and ability, and I am afraid that I will not be able to handle it. However, due to the urging of the central government and Chairman Huang, I have no choice but to reluctantly go. President Wang said that the Republic of China is composed of five ethnic groups: Han, Manchu, Mongolian, Hui, and Tibetan. In the past, Tibet had a deep relationship with the mainland. Although there was some estrangement in the middle, it has gradually been eliminated recently. Now, the central government has no so-called policies or methods for the local areas, only sincerity, that is, the central government sincerely protects and helps the local areas. This is true not only for Tibet, but also for Mongolia and the mainland. He instructed me to convey this meaning when I meet with the local authorities in Tibet after entering Tibet. I will leave Beijing for Qinghai at the end of the month and arrive in Qinghai on the 10th of next month, and then depart with the Panchen Lama. The earliest I can return to Beijing is next summer. (9th Special Dispatch)

United States Plans to Conclude Agreement with China on Transporting Naval Mailbags 47

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications notified the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 9th that the U.S. Postal Authorities intend to renew an agreement with the Chinese Postal Authorities on the transportation of naval mailbags. According to the General Postal Administration, the International Postal Convention stipulates that warships stationed overseas may exchange sealed mailbags, but only for letters. Parcels are not included in this regulation. In recent years, the general postal mailbags exchanged between U.S. warships and the U.S. Navy stationed in various parts of China have included parcels. This is clearly inconsistent with the provisions of the convention. The request to conclude an agreement is difficult to comply with for two reasons: First, the mailing of parcels requires customs inspection and taxation, but the sealed warship mailbags are not subject to customs inspection. If parcels are sealed in warship mailbags, the customs procedures that should be followed cannot be completed. The postal service has no right to agree to this. Second, parcels for domestic delivery can be mailed from post offices across the country, so there is no need to seal them in naval mailbags. (9th Special Dispatch)

Chaoshan: Implementation of Soybean Cake Surtax; Shantou Merchants Have Passively Gone on Strike 84

Shantou Communication: The provincial government has recently implemented a soybean cake tax, which is contracted by merchants to the Department of Finance in the name of a joint company. The company is called the "Lian'an Company, Contractor of the Additional Construction Fee of Sun Yat-sen University on Imported Cake Fertilizers for the Entire Guangdong Province," and it has undertaken to pay an annual fee of 500,060 yuan. The Lian'an Company has sent personnel to Shantou to establish the Chao-Mei Collection Office, appointing Du Ridong as the head and Wei Cuiming as his deputy. The tax collection is scheduled to begin on September 2nd. A notice has been issued to inform the grain brokers of the North and South ports. The notice states, "It has been decided that an additional fee of 25 cents per dan will be levied on imported soybean cake fertilizer for the construction fee of Sun Yat-sen University, as announced by the Guangdong Finance Special Commissioner's Office. The tax collection is scheduled to begin on September 2nd, and 16 Shangheng Road has been selected as the Chao-Mei District Collection Office. All merchants transporting soybean cake into this city must first send the invoice and customs declaration to this sub-office for verification and pay the fee according to the quantity, and obtain a certificate before they can transport it by ship, train, or boat. When transferring, a declaration should be made, and a transfer certificate should be obtained, and the fee certificate should be affixed to the invoice in order to comply with the procedures. Soybean cake transported before September will be exempted from fees, but the quantity transported to various counties must be listed and registered in order to issue a transit permit; otherwise, it will be investigated and punished as leakage. As this is the beginning of the operation, it is feared that merchants may not be aware, so it is necessary to explain in detail to avoid mistakes. It is of utmost importance that all merchants comply with the above regulations and avoid penalties. This notice." After the notice was issued, merchants and people were shocked, because soybean cake is the main fertilizer. For years the farmland in Chaozhou and Meizhou feel application imported fertilizer powder fail, and all plantings use soybean cake as the sole raw material. Therefore, in the corner of Chao-Mei alone, more than seven million pieces of cake are used each year. Now, if a tax is uniformly levied, the rural villages of Chao-Mei will suddenly face an increased burden of more than 800,000 yuan, which is not in line with the government's intention to protect farmers and merchants. The Grain Association held a general meeting of all members on the 2nd to discuss countermeasures, and soybean cake merchants in Shanghai and Wuhan believe that this industry is in its infancy, and domestic cake factories must rely on the government's support and encouragement to develop. Donation merchants are only interested in profit, and they are not aware of the overall situation. They are no different from promoting the sales of imported products and will leave domestic products without any chance of survival. Therefore, they expressed dissatisfaction with this matter and have jointly implemented a strike pending a resolution. The North-South Port Cargo Transportation Association also convened a meeting to discuss countermeasures after the tax on soybean cake was implemented: (1) Request the government not to be deceived by the donor merchants and cancel the case to benefit farmers and merchants; otherwise, they will not stop; (2) All colleagues should report to the association before September 1st the number of soybean cakes they have ordered from other ports and the cake number must be noted; (3) If the donation merchant interferes with soybean cakes transported en route, they should be allowed to register them at their discretion, but the fee should not be paid immediately to facilitate negotiations; (4) Because this matter is of great importance, 15 people have been elected as executive members to be responsible for handling it. The association also sent Rao Dongming to negotiate with the donation merchant, requesting to postpone the opening of the tax on soybean cake imported after September 1st and to make temporary registration first, pending the resolution of the negotiation with the province, and then decide whether to pay. The donation merchant claimed that it would not be accepted because it related to the source of funds, and that it was impossible for Shantou to avoid it because the province had already implemented it. However, a certain foreigner became very active because of this incident and raised funds to open the Japan-Manchuria Products Co., Ltd., each share of which is 100 yuan, and Chinese are also allowed to subscribe. It is currently in progress, and it is planned to smuggle soybean cake from Dalian to Shantou for sale, seizing the market. From then on, the soybean cake industry may follow in the footsteps of oil and rice and fall into the hands of certain foreigners.

Suzhou: Suspected Case of a Car Crushing a Road Worker to Death

Since the opening of the Suzhou-Changshu Highway, there have been no unfortunate incidents. However, the other day late at night, Chen Hailin, a road worker from Shandong, was lying across the road near Lumu to cool off when a dark blue car speeding from Changshu through Suzhou crushed Chen Hailin to death. After other road workers learned of this, the car that caused the accident was nowhere to be found. The area in charge of the area reported the matter to the local court, which sent personnel to inspect the scene the following afternoon. It was confirmed that Chen Hailin had been crushed to death by a car. The third branch of the Public Security Bureau discovered a dark blue car near Penglai World on Liuyuan Road on the afternoon of the 8th. There was no one in the car, and the license plate had been removed, so there was no way to investigate who the owner of the car was. The Public Security Bureau is investigating the origin of the car. According to nearby people, there were five or six passengers in the car when it came to Suzhou, and they have disappeared after injuring people. Some say that the car may have been involved in a kidnapping.

Commemoration of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's First Uprising: Yesterday's General Assembly; More Than One Hundred Representatives from All Walks of Life Attended; Huang Gaoxiong Reported on the Significance of the Commemoration 85

According to the Central News Agency, September 9th is the anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's first uprising in Guangdong. The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters convened representatives from all walks of life in the city at the Grand Auditorium at 10:00 AM to hold the 40th anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's first uprising and notified all sectors to hang flags to celebrate. The details of the commemoration meeting are recorded below:

Participating Representatives

The representatives who attended included Huang Gaoxiong from the Municipal Party Headquarters Committee, Du Mengsen from the Cooperative Enterprise Promotion Association, Zhu Shide from the China National Products Maintenance Association, Sun Xuanhuan from the Pearl and Jade Industry Guild, Tan Gengxin from the Shanghai Audit Office of the Audit Department, Zhao Zhenhui from the Pharmaceutical Industry Guild, Zhang Lichun from the Municipal Education Association, Tang Chongshi from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Xuan Bokun from Qingnian Middle School, Dong Chongshan from the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, Ma Hanfeng from the Labor Education Association, Yu Yaoqiu from the Baoshan Fellow Townsmen Association, and more than one hundred representatives from various schools and party headquarters at all levels.

Chairman Reports The meeting was presided over by Huang Gaoxiong, chairman of the Municipal Committee, and the ceremony was conducted according to the rules. The chairman reported on the significance of the commemoration, stating that today is the anniversary of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's first uprising in Guangdong, and forty years have passed since Dr. Sun Yat-sen's first uprising. During these forty years, there have been several changes in Chinese politics, but this is the first glorious anniversary in the history of Chinese revival. Since this uprising, the Chinese National Revolution has established a foundation. At that time, the domestic government was corrupt, and foreign imperialism was actively invading China. During this period, China was on the brink of extreme danger, so an uprising and revolution were necessary to save it. Dr. Sun resolutely decided to unite comrades, and was extremely brave and willing to sacrifice, but because the organization was not strict and the number of people was small, it still failed. However, since then, the Chinese people have understood the purpose of the revolution, and the revolutionary forces spread everywhere have gradually expanded. The actions of the revolution have become more active, and the success of the Xinhai Revolution cannot be said to have not started on this day. However, looking at the current domestic situation and tracing back to Dr. Sun's spirit of fighting for the revolution, we should have the following points of feeling: (1) In the future revolution, we must earnestly follow Dr. Sun's principles; (2) Internal organization should strive for strictness; (3) Domestic spiritual unity, unanimous opposition to the outside world, and all construction work should be based on the spirit of hard work. After the chairman's report, slogans were shouted, and the meeting was adjourned.

Commemorative Slogans

(1) Dr. Sun's uprising is the pioneer of the revival of the Chinese nation; (2) Dr. Sun's uprising is a revolutionary action against autocratic politics; (3) Emulate Dr. Sun's great personality; (4) Inherit Dr. Sun's revolutionary spirit; (5) Fulfill Dr. Sun's will; (6) Long live the Three Principles of the People; (7) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang; (8) Long live the Republic of China.

Postal General Bureau: A Bold Robbery Yesterday Resulted in a Huge Loss; Bandits Fled with Pistols and Mausers After the Heist; 91,930 Yuan Stolen; Yuan Bingshu and Lu Ruilin Dead, Zhou Yucheng Wounded; Police Authorities Intensifying Investigation, Aiming to Solve the Case Shortly 86

Yesterday morning at approximately 10:00 AM, a robbery occurred at the Postal General Bureau on the bank of the Suzhou Creek on North Sichuan Road in this city. The bandits fatally shot one clerk and one guard from the bureau, and wounded another guard. The total amount stolen reached 91,930 yuan. The details of the incident are described below:

Following the Usual Morning Escort of Funds

According to established practice, the Postal General Bureau in this city daily sends funds to the Postal Remittance and Savings Bureau at No. 53 Fuzhou Road for deposit. For security, the Savings Bureau dispatches an armored car and two guards around 9:00 AM each morning to collect the funds. Yesterday, being Monday, the bureau followed the usual procedure, sending a car (Municipal License 12442, Concession License 16182) and guards, Lu Ruilin from Hubei and Zhou Yucheng from Shandong, to the General Bureau to collect the funds. At the General Bureau, the cash exchange and collection office prepared the funds collected from Saturday and Sunday, totaling 91,920 yuan, packed and sealed them securely in a mailbag, and ordered Yuan Bingshu, a clerk, to carry it downstairs to the car in the courtyard.

Clerk Shot Down, Silver Bag Snatched

Unexpectedly, as Yuan Bingshu walked halfway down the stairs, two bandits suddenly emerged from the corner with guns, ordering Yuan to drop the bag. The clerk, realizing the danger, quickly tried to escape, but a gunshot rang out behind him, hitting Yuan in the lower abdomen. He fell to the cement floor beside the stairs. The two bandits quickly rushed forward, grabbed the silver bag, and fled through the small door leading to Tiantong Road to the north. At this time, guards Lu Ruilin and Zhou Yucheng were waiting by the money transport car. Suddenly hearing gunshots and seeing two bandits carrying guns and fleeing with the loot, they knew something was wrong and quickly drew their pistols, intending to fire at the fleeing bandits. However, bandits had been lying in ambush near the car. Seeing the two guards drawing guns, the bandits immediately opened fire on the guards from behind. Lu Ruilin and Zhou Yucheng, caught off guard, quickly ran into the guard room to take cover, engaging in a fierce gun battle with the bandits from behind the wall.

Barrage of Bullets, Guards Fall

Amid a barrage of bullets, the guards, unexpectedly, were unharmed. Seeing that the two guards were running out of ammunition, they chased into the guard room, firing at Lu and Zhou. Consequently, Lu Ruilin and Zhou Yucheng were both hit, bullets entering their abdomens, and they fell inside the room. The bandits then fired over ten shots into the air before leaving, also fleeing through the small door to the north. The bureau's patrol officers chased after them, firing as they went, until they reached Tiantong Road. The bandits then jumped into a taxi (Concession License 17671) waiting next to the New Asia Hotel and sped northeast. A large number of detectives from the Hongkou Police Station arrived at the scene after receiving the alarm, but the bandits' car had already escaped.

One Dead, One Wounded Despite Treatment

The police quickly returned to the station and notified the fire brigade to send an ambulance to the Postal General Bureau. Yuan, Lu, and Zhou were taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Unfortunately, Yuan Bingshu's wounds were fatal, and he died en route to the hospital. Lu Ruilin was shot twice, bullets entering his abdomen and waist. Zhou Yucheng was shot twice, one bullet hitting his liver and the other his intestines. Lu Ruilin's condition deteriorated rapidly, and he also died at 2:00 PM. Zhou Yucheng, with a bullet in his abdomen, underwent surgery to remove the bullet, but his injuries were too severe, and his condition remained critical.

Investigating the Bandits' Taxi

The Hongkou Police Station immediately telegraphed all police agencies in the city for assistance after the incident. They also reported to the Central Police Station to trace the origin of the bandits' car. It was later learned that the car belonged to the Dalei Taxi Company at No. 148 North Sichuan Road. Detectives were immediately dispatched to investigate. It was reported that around 8:40 AM that morning, a man wearing a dark blue silk long gown and a straw hat, approximately twenty years old, had rented the car. He stated that he was going to the Municipal Government Health Bureau and then to Jiangwan, agreeing to a fare of three yuan, paying a deposit of two yuan in advance. The company's accountant then ordered driver Kong Xianrong, a native of Yangzhou, to drive the car (Municipal License 4743, Concession License 17671).

Driver Bound, Bandits Drive Themselves

After the man got into the car, he ordered the driver to drive north. When the car reached the first bridge on Qimei Road, three other men wearing long gowns and short jackets got into the car. They immediately pulled out Mauser pistols, forbade the driver from making any noise, bound him with hemp rope, and pushed him out of the car. The four men then drove the car themselves south. Later, a passerby noticed and untied him. Kong quickly ran to the Linping Road Police Station to report the incident and telegraphed the taxi company. Before long, news of the robbery arrived. The police station then notified the Hongkou Police Station and took the driver in for questioning, while also ordering all detectives to be on the lookout for the car.

Intensified Investigation, Aiming for Quick Resolution

Around 1:40 PM, the car was discovered at the end of Tianbao Road in Zhabei. The Linping Road Police Station notified the Hongkou Police Station, which sent detectives to jointly inspect the scene, examine the traces in the car, and take them back for filing. The Dalei Taxi Company was then notified to retrieve the car around 3:00 PM. At the scene of the incident, the police collected several bullet casings and took them back for examination. They also dispatched additional detectives and all on-duty police officers to conduct investigations, aiming to solve the case as soon as possible. According to witnesses, the bandits were mostly wearing long gowns and spoke the dialects of Funing and Yancheng. However, their movements during the robbery were calm and methodical, suggesting they were well-organized. The bodies of the deceased clerk Yuan Bingshu and guard Lu Ruilin have been transferred from the hospital to the coroner's office. The Postal General Bureau and the Savings Bureau are currently handling their funeral arrangements. In addition to reporting the incident to the authorities and pursuing the criminals, the issue of compensation for the deceased is also under discussion.

Concrete Decisions Reached on the Factory Inspection Issue; Shanghai Municipal Government to Continue Negotiations with Concession Authorities; Tang Jianfei Returned to Beijing Yesterday Afternoon to Report on His Mission 89

According to Dagong News Agency, the unresolved issue of factory inspections in the Shanghai concessions has been dragging on. This year, our representatives raised the issue at the International Labour Conference and gained international understanding. The Central Government specially dispatched Tang Jianfei, Director of the Labour Department of the Ministry of Industry, to Shanghai to consult with the Municipal Government on the steps to continue negotiations. Mr. Tang completed his mission in Shanghai and returned to Beijing by train yesterday afternoon to report on his mission. According to Mr. Tang, before his departure, he told a reporter from Dagong News Agency that the issue of factory inspections in the Shanghai concessions is unique. The issue of sovereignty involves several countries, including England, France, the United States, Japan, and Italy. Although the factories are located in the concessions, the right to conduct inspections to ensure worker safety belongs to China in terms of reason and justice. However, the lack of understanding from the authorities of various countries stationed in Shanghai has resulted in the negotiations remaining unresolved. The Ministry of Industry, in order to earnestly implement the Labour Law in accordance with the Central Government's order, believes that it is necessary to resolve this outstanding issue quickly. Since international sympathy and understanding have been obtained at this year's International Labour Conference, he was specially ordered to come to Shanghai to discuss the steps and methods for continuing negotiations with the Municipal Government in order to proceed at an opportune moment. He arrived in Shanghai on the 7th and invited Cheng Haifeng, Director of the Chinese Branch of the International Labour Organization, to visit Secretary-General Yu of the Municipal Government for several consultations. Concrete decisions have been reached, and it is only necessary for the Municipal Government to continue negotiations with the concession authorities. It is expected that a satisfactory resolution will be reached soon. His mission has been completed, and he needs to return to Beijing to report on his mission. If necessary, he will return to Shanghai.

Distressed Overseas Chinese from Belgium Return to China, Arriving in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; A Total of Thirty-One People Were Forced to Leave the Country 90

Due to the global economic downturn in recent years, overseas Chinese residing abroad have been repeatedly oppressed by foreign countries, suffering hardships that are difficult to describe. Those who have returned to China one after another are often seen. Yesterday morning, the German OolerBremen freight ship Alai arrived in port, carrying thirty-one overseas Chinese from Belgium to Shanghai, in a rather miserable state. The details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai

The ship docked at Huangpu Wharf at 7:00 AM yesterday morning. After disembarking, the overseas Chinese were guided by personnel from the relief section of the Public Security Bureau to temporarily reside at the Dongfang Hotel in Xiaodongmen. They were in a very wretched condition. Upon hearing the news, the Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau sent Hou Can and Tan Zhonglu to express their sympathy. However, they were penniless and in dire straits, urgently awaiting practical relief from the authorities to avoid becoming starving corpses.

List of Distressed Overseas Chinese

The overseas Chinese who arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning included Lin Dipu, Chen Tinglian, Ji Shangyuan, Chen Zhixiu, Xu Hongguang, Jin Daan, Jin Tiyuan, Ji Shuxiang, Wu Cheng, Wang Jinting, Zhuo Chengwu, Wang Guanzong, Sun Shuidian, Fu Bosen, Xia Liangqing, Ji Yanlian, Chen Zhifu, Chen Guikai, Zhuo Jinxiong, Jin Fengen, Yang Guocai, Lin Qingtao, Ye Zhanglian, Zhou Meicai, Liu Junyi, Ni Zhikui and his wife (Belgian) and two young children. Except for Fu Bosen and Zhuo Jinxiong, who are from Wenzhou, Zhejiang, the rest are from Qingtian, Zhejiang. There were also Liu Weifan from Hubei and Jiang Guojie from Jiangsu, who were students in Belgium, and were also forced to return, totaling twenty-one people.

Reasons for Forced Departure

Lin Di, a representative of the distressed overseas Chinese, told a reporter from the Industry and Commerce News that they had been living in Belgium for many years, mostly running small businesses, with a considerable history. Unexpectedly, Belgium was also affected by the economic downturn. With a sharp increase in the number of unemployed people in the country, the government, in order to settle the general unemployed population, used the pretext of checking passports that did not conform to the requirements to force them to leave the country. Ling Qihan, our country's acting minister to Belgium, negotiated with the Belgian government several times, but to no avail. As a last resort, Ling Qihan arranged to purchase ship tickets on their behalf. On July 23rd, they boarded the German OolerBremen freight ship Alai in Hnese, Belgium, passing through the Netherlands, Italy, the Suez Canal, the Indian Ocean, Little Luzon, Singapore, and Hong Kong before arriving in Shanghai.

Planning Relief Efforts

Before leaving Belgium, the thirty-one distressed overseas Chinese had been telegraphed to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs by the embassy in Belgium. After learning about the situation, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs informed the Shanghai Municipal Government and ordered the relief section of the Public Security Bureau to provide relief. The registration process was immediately started to provide appropriate relief. It is now learned that, in addition to covering hotel expenses, the authorities are also planning to arrange ship tickets to send them back to their hometowns.

The Distressed Overseas Chinese from Belgium Who Returned to Shanghai Yesterday (Photo by Industry and Commerce News)

Today they will go to Hangzhou to then Suzhou, and finally to Beijing to attend the meeting, this newspaper reports. The Guangdong Provincial delegation, including Xie Yingzhou, President of the Guangdong Provincial High Court, Pan Guanying, Chief Clerk, Qian Yao, Prosecutor, and representatives from Zhongshan University and Lingnan University Law Schools, a group of five, arrived in Shanghai yesterday after taking the Empress of Japan from Hong Kong on the 6th. They are scheduled to take the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Hangzhou this morning. Two days later, they will travel to Suzhou to investigate the judicial situation. They are scheduled to travel to Beijing along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway on the 14th to attend the National Judicial Conference. Around the end of this month, they will return to Guangdong by boat.

Since the oil cake and miscellaneous grain merchants opposed the Guangdong Province's increase in the bran tax, they have collectively suspended operations and transportation. The three J.U. number Junkers-style large aircraft newly borrowed by the Eurasia Aviation Company from Germany had one which was flown out of Germany on the 3rd of this month by the famous aviator Lude. End of September and End of October Approaching Rapidly; Various Industries Preparing to Find Ways to Weather the Storm; Money Trade Opens Experience Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Reforms; Also Holds Executive Committee Meeting to Prepare for Re-election 94

The end of September, the settlement period for commercial accounts, and the end of October, the long-term loan period for the money trade, are rapidly approaching. The Money Trade Association held an autumn experience meeting yesterday to discuss business and reforms, and also held the 47th meeting of the second executive committee to prepare for the second re-election. The details are as follows:

Money Trade Autumn Experience Meeting

The Money Trade Association held an autumn experience meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon in the Inner Garden of the South City. Managers from 55 companies, including Fu Yuan, Shen Yuan, Rui Chang, Yi Chang, Fu Kang, Zi Kang, Zi Feng, Hong Feng, Dou Chang, Bin Feng, Qing Cheng, Da De, Zhi Yu, Yi Da, Shun Kang, Dun Yu, Tong Yu, Tong Run, Da Mai, Yuan Sheng, Ren Chang, Hui Feng, Zhen Tai, and Cheng Yu, and Pei Yunqing, Liu Wuqiao, etc., attended. Qin Runqing presided over the meeting, and Ge Huaiqing took the minutes. First, the chairman reported on the state of decline of the money trade and various industries. Then, they exchanged views on matters that should be promoted and reformed within the money trade. The long-term credit loans due at the end of October were also discussed, but no decisions were made. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 PM.

Executive Committee Meeting to Prepare for Re-election

The 47th meeting of the second executive committee, originally scheduled to be held today, was held early yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Members Qin Runqing, Li Shoushan, Pei Yunqing, Liu Wuqiao, Zhang Mengzhou, Xi Jiming, Yan Dayou, Zheng Bingquan, Qian Yuansheng, etc., attended. Qin Runqing presided over the meeting, and Ge Huaiqing took the minutes. First, the chairman reported that the term of office of the executive committee members of the association had expired and that the re-election was scheduled to take place at the members' representative meeting on October 2nd. The current executive committee members were asked to be responsible for preparing for the re-election. A resolution was passed, and the meeting adjourned at 4:30 PM. The committee members also toured the famous scenic spots in the Inner Garden.

Busy Settlement in September

The settlement period for industry and commerce was originally divided into the Dragon Boat Festival, the Mid-Autumn Festival, and the year-end settlement period for the Lunar New Year's Eve. After the adoption of the Gregorian calendar, the settlement period was divided into the end of June, the end of September, and the year-end settlement period for the end of January. The settlement period for the end of September this year is rapidly approaching. Companies and businesses are sending people to collect outstanding payments from various customers. They are busy with settlements these days and are issuing invoices. Since the implementation of the 5 million yuan in industrial and commercial credit loans, Shanghai's industry and commerce will be able to weather the settlement period at the end of September. At that time, the receipts and payments of the money and silver trades will inevitably be busier, as companies and businesses return outstanding payments to banks and money shops after receiving payment.

Various Industries Prepare for Long-Term Loans in October

Long-term credit loans in the money trade were originally divided into the end of March and the end of September. After the adoption of the Gregorian calendar, it became the end of April and the end of October. At the end of April this year, a small financial panic occurred due to the economic downturn in the city. Fortunately, the government made every effort to provide relief, and it was quelled. The end of October is rapidly approaching, and various money shops have made considerable preparations for this. Moreover, the cooperation between the silver and money trades has been quite effective, so there is no cause for concern.

Sino-Japanese Telephone Call Continued Yesterday Morning; Tan Weixue Went to the United States Yesterday to Negotiate Sino-American Telephone Call 95

According to Dagong News Agency, the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications conducted another test call with Tokyo, Japan yesterday morning. The signal was clear and even better than before. Arakawa, a representative from the Japanese Ministry of Communications, came to China to negotiate matters related to the telephone call, and has already returned to Japan after graduating. Tan Weixue, Vice President of Shanghai Telephone Company, who was sent to the United States by the Ministry of Communications to negotiate the Sino-American telephone call, took a boat to the United States yesterday morning. The details are as follows:

Arakawa Returns to Japan

Arakawa, Director of the Tokyo Telephone Bureau, was specially dispatched by the Japanese Ministry of Communications to China to negotiate matters related to Sino-Japanese wireless communication. He arrived in China by boat on the 25th of last month. After consulting with Wen Yuqing, Director of the International Telecommunications Bureau, he went to Beijing to meet with Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Communications, and Yan Renguang, Director of the Telecommunications Administration, to discuss all important procedures for telephone calls between the two countries. After returning to Shanghai, he had a final consultation with the relevant radio station authorities in China. Arakawa has completed his mission in China and returned to Japan by boat the day before yesterday to report on the progress.

Sino-Japanese Test Call

The International Telecommunications Bureau and the International Radio Station in this city, under the order of the Ministry of Communications, are actively preparing for Sino-Japanese wireless telephone calls. Therefore, the person in charge of the bureau has repeatedly conducted tests. In the beginning, there were occasional obstacles affecting the signal. After further research on machinery and technology, they resumed the test call with Tokyo, Japan, yesterday morning from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM, still using the terminal of the Liuhang receiving station. As a result, significant progress was made in signal technology. It is planned to conduct the final test on Thursday and Friday of this week. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications is responsible for connecting the Chinese user's master terminal with the Liuhang radio station terminal line, which is expected to be completed soon. Therefore, the Sino-Japanese telephone call is expected to be imminent.

Tan Goes to America

Tan Weixue, Vice President of the Shanghai Telephone Company, was recently ordered by the Ministry of Communications to go to the United States to negotiate matters related to telephone calls between China and the United States. Tan has applied for leave from the Shanghai Telephone Company and packed his bags. He set sail on the Changxing Company's Empress of Japan at 5:00 AM yesterday morning. His relatives and friends went to see him off.

The original letter from the Nanjing Minzhong Education Hall is also attached below. To the editor, in the summer of the 22nd year, for the purpose of assisting the volunteers, this hall held a charity painting and calligraphy exhibition, collecting works from famous artists for a lottery sale. The proceeds were 465 yuan. After deducting 63 yuan for mounting painting costs, the net balance was 402 yuan. At the end of the exhibition, the volunteers had all disbanded, so the funds did not need to be remitted. It was discussed at the 66th meeting of the hall's affairs committee, and it was agreed that the proceeds from the sale of famous artists' works for the purpose of assisting the volunteers should be handled with caution. It was decided to build a building related to national humiliation on the vacant land within the hall to leave a permanent memorial. However, just as the proposal was being finalized, this hall was ordered to relocate, so the construction could not be carried out

Relief is Saving Lives - Donate One More Penny, Save One More Life. immediately. It has been almost two years since the postponement. Although there is no definite date for the relocation of this hall, construction is still difficult to start. At this time, the flood is spreading across the two regions of the Yangtze and Yellow Rivers, and the number of starving and drowning compatriots exceeds tens of millions. Donating to relief efforts is the duty of everyone. Moreover, moving the funds from assisting the volunteers to relieving the affected compatriots is an act of patriotism and saving the people. It is believed that it will be supported by the famous artists who donated the works. Therefore, it was decided at the 81st meeting of the hall's affairs committee to donate all 426 yuan of the principal and interest from the sale of the charity painting and calligraphy exhibition to the National Flood Relief Association to relieve the victims. The 426 yuan donation has been remitted by the Bank of Communications and is requested to be forwarded, and a receipt is requested. In addition to a special letter stating the process of the donation, it is hoped that it will be published in your newspaper to facilitate widespread knowledge, and please forward this letter to the Flood Relief Association as a basis. The Curator of Jiangsu Provincial Nanjing Minzhong Education Hall, Zhu Jianbai, September 6th.
