Free Talk

Preface to "Collected Essays of Tui Bei" 180

— Tang Tao

Here are my seventy-odd essays.

I began to think about writing in the spring of 1933. At that time, I had just suffered the loss of my father and was struggling under the burden of life. Grieving, exhausted, and lonely, I often wanted to find a way to vent. Because I was living alone, I had few people to chat with, so I would flip through the Shen Bao and read the "Free Talk" section.

That's how I got the idea of submitting articles.

But I didn't start writing right away. It wasn't until the end of May that I was urged to repay part of the debt my father had left me. Letters kept coming from home, telling me about the coldness of relatives, the alienation of my father's friends, and the bullying of villagers since my father's death. Then my mother went blind in her right eye. A myriad of arrows pierced my young heart. I couldn't escape. I stayed in my lodgings, listening to the incessant rain, feeling extremely desolate and angry.

But I could still only read "Free Talk."

The rain continued to fall, and I grew more and more grieved and angry. The only way to comfort myself seemed to be to think about the past and then write it down on paper and send it to "Free Talk." A few days later, it was actually published. This was my first article, which is also included in this collection, "Rain in My Hometown."

And so I became a contributor to "Free Talk."

But I didn't bring my own grief and anger to the page. At first, what I wrote was mostly about reminiscing, idle chats, and records of events. Sometimes I would also touch on literary circles or current affairs, and my tone was straightforward. I didn't know anything about taboos, and it was all very childish.

Later, I also submitted articles to other publications. The articles here were mostly published in "Free Talk," "Torch," "Tai Bai," "New Yu Lin," "Human World," "Reading Life," "Trends," "Yu Lin," and other places. But it's not all of them. Many have been lost, and some have been deliberately deleted.

I write very slowly, often revising again and again. If I were to put it nicely, it would be that I'm very careful. But sometimes, being too careful causes problems, and I've even caused some misunderstandings as a result. But misunderstandings are just that. They don't have much of an impact on me.

Just like my background, I'm still a rough guy, and one with a bit of youthful spirit at that.

In recent years, we have often seen middle-aged and older people playing strange tricks. Humor has long been established, and collections of jokes have already been published. They play with antiques, drink good tea, write frivolous poems, read Zhuangzi, recommend the Wen Xuan, and write seal script couplets. Those who are less capable even promote the reading of classics and the revival of classical Chinese. This is called being tired of living. But it's the young people who suffer. Because they themselves are tired of living, they try to persuade young people to learn to be mature and pretend to be leisurely. Even children around ten years old are not spared. How many pure and useful minds in elementary school are being ruined into fossils by reading classics!

In these situations, I am willing to open my throat and oppose it with all my might. It's not because I'm still young and the issue is particularly relevant to me. It's really because in the last two years, the path left for young people to take has been too difficult. Big and small responsibilities are always placed on the shoulders of young people! But when they really take them up, this one says "not right," that one says "not so," and some even say "not allowed." Loving freshness requires telling lies, and being unemployed is a sign of high standards and weak abilities. Think about it, my teachers, where is the road?

But there is a road, and it must be forged by young people themselves.

My articles sometimes appear in the seats of gentlemen—in publications that promote leisure. But I only sell my articles, not myself, so many of my opinions are still rough. But in the world, there is only one self. Gentlemen are allowed to have a self, but rough guys are not, and their fate is to be deleted.

This makes me afraid to go to the gentlemen's seats again.

The essays I have collected in this book are up to the end of March of this year.

Looking at it, it's the plum rain season again. My mood is still the same as it was two years ago—grief, exhaustion, and loneliness. But this time, I'm not shrinking back so much.

Calling this book "Collected Essays of Tui Bei" doesn't have any deep meaning, and it's not to say that my articles will predict anything. According to legend, when Li Chunfeng and Yuan Tiangang were making the Tui Bei Tu, Yuan pushed Li's back to stop him at the sixtieth diagram. That's where the name Tui Bei Tu comes from. I'm only writing a few essays now and haven't concerned myself with future generations. But I often feel that someone is pushing my back to stop me. Well, now I've compiled these seventy-odd pieces into a collection, and that's finally a small ending. If I have to say that "Collected Essays of Tui Bei" has any meaning, then that's my meaning!

(Postscript) "Collected Essays of Tui Bei" will be published by Tianma Bookstore and is currently in print. It will be available to readers within half a month.

The Metamorphosis of the "Orange" (Part 2) 181

— Chen Zizhan

In Hunan, near Dongting Lake, has always been famous for producing oranges. However, some say that Wei Yingwu's line "Dongting must wait for the frost to fill the forest" refers to the Dongting Mountain in Taihu Lake, because he once served as the governor of Suzhou, so his poem mentions it. At the same time, we can cite some evidence regarding the production of oranges in Dongting Mountain, such as Wang Wei's poem to a friend going to Yuezhou, "Wind ferries Ruoye Road, frost bridges Dongting autumn." Also, Su Zimei's Gusu poem has the line "Dongting tangerines are ripe, guests share gold." According to ancient geography books, the Dongting Lake of Chu has a subterranean passage to the Dongting Mountain of Wu, so it is called Dongting. Fanciful myths, of course, are unreliable. However, the same production of oranges in both places has the record of the ancients to rely on. The Classic of Mountains and Seas says "The mountain of Dongting, its trees are mostly oranges." I don't remember clearly whether it was in Chu or Wu. Also, according to the Xiangyang Records, "Li Shuping, on his deathbed, instructed his son, 'In Longyang Continent, there are a thousand wooden slaves, and when the tangerines and oranges ripen, you will get a thousand bolts of silk per year.'" Longyang is now Hanshou in Hunan. Zhang Hua of the Jin Dynasty said, "Oranges are on the side of the lake, and people of low status do not spread them." Liu Jinchen's Ode to the Orange says, "Living in Southern Chu." Xie Huilian's Ode to the Mandarin Orange says, "I am entrusted to the district of the lake." Also, in the third year of Chongning in the Song Dynasty, the Great Liao envoy Xie gave a table of mandarin oranges, saying: "The fragrance fills the sleeves, dyeing the clear frost of the Xiang River. The cloud liquid fills the plate, drawing the remaining moisture of Dongting." It can be seen that Hunan has always produced oranges, and Dongting oranges are a very valuable fruit.

If the Tribute of Yu says, "The Huai and Hai region is only Yangzhou, its oranges and pomelos are offered in tribute," and Yangzhou indeed includes the present-day areas of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Zhejiang, and Fujian, then we can examine the wide area of orange production in ancient China. Also, Zuo Si's Rhapsody on the Capital of Shu has "Households have gardens of oranges and pomelos," which proves that Sichuan also produced oranges in ancient times. The Records of Strange Things says: "Giao Chi has a mandarin orange official, with a rank of two hundred shi, in charge of the annual tribute of imperial oranges." Also, the Accounts of Strange Things says: "The more mandarin oranges are drawn, the more bridge taxes there are." Since the Han Dynasty, what has been called Giao Chi and Southern Yue is now the area of ​​Guangdong and Guangxi, and also includes part of Annam. This place was naturally the place with the most orange production in the Han Dynasty. Originally, oranges like warmth and fear cold, and are most suitable for growing in the south. The best ones grow in the Pearl River basin, the second best grow south of the Yangtze River, and the species will change when grown north of the river. I remember that Yanzi's Spring and Autumn Annals said, "The mandarin orange becomes a tangerine when born south of the Huai River, and a trifoliate orange when born north of the Huai River. The leaves are similar, but the taste of the fruit is different. Why is this? The water and soil are different." The Records of Natural History also says, "An orange crossing the river transforms into a trifoliate orange." The Materia Medica has trifoliate orange peels, saying, "The people of Jiangzuo call it Wu stinky oranges." Also, Pan Anren made a poem for Jia Mi to give to Lu Ji, saying, "It is called a tangerine in the south, and an orange when crossing north." The tangerine cannot cross north either.

Oranges and tangerines are two different fruits, but the ancients often did not distinguish them clearly. The words of the ancients about oranges quoted above often involve tangerines. Dongpo's Collection has a poem about Liu Jingwen's collection of Wang Zijing's posts, saying that "Your family has two lines of twelve characters, and the spirit overwhelms Ye Hou's ten thousand rooms." Dongpo Jushi once said, "It is said that Wang Zijing's post has the words 'Three hundred yellow tangerines.' This post is in the house of Liu Jisun Jingwen. Jingwen died, and I don't know whose house it is in now." It was originally Wang Youjun Yizhi's post, but Dongpo mistakenly thought it was Wang Daling Xianzhi's post; it was originally three hundred mandarin oranges offered, but Dongpo mistakenly thought it was three hundred yellow tangerines; however, it is not only Dongpo who made the mistake of not distinguishing tangerines and oranges. In Hunan, not only are finger-like Buddha's hand tangerines and bowl-sized pomelos clearly distinguished, but jiu, which are only for ornamental purposes, are also clearly distinguished. Tangerines and oranges are different, and they are also different from oranges. Tangerine peels are yellow and not red, and have a stinky smell, or are called Ao-skinned tangerines, and are sour and not sweet. Oranges are larger than tangerines and smaller than pomelos. The skin is green and not red, like bergamot, but it is not fragrant and cannot be eaten. However, Xinhui oranges and Wenzhou tangerines are delicious, and it can certainly be said that "the water and soil are different!"

Wenzhou tangerines are slightly bitter, but there is sweetness in the bitterness, and the taste is not bad. When Han Yanzhi of the Song Dynasty was an official in Wenzhou, he wrote a Mandarin Orange Record, the first volume saying oranges and tangerines, the middle volume saying oranges, and the last volume saying planting methods. Tangerines are a famous product of Wenzhou, and it can be said that there is a book specifically for them. Some say that Xinhui oranges are just tangerines because Cantonese people call tangerines sweet oranges and call honey oranges tangerines, so there is a distinction between tall oranges and flat tangerines. I think Guangdong honey oranges are better than Siamese honey oranges, but the taste of Fujian honey oranges is similar to that of Hunan oranges. Although Nanfeng honey oranges are small, the taste is not bad. The smallest is Ji'an golden oranges, which are even smaller than pigeon eggs. The taste is in the skin. Ouyang Xiu's Returning to the Fields Record says: "Golden oranges are produced in Jiangxi, and are transported from afar. The people of the capital did not know them at first. At the beginning of Mingdao Jingyou, they first came to the capital with bamboo shoots. The bamboo shoots tasted sour, and people did not like them very much. Then they were no longer produced. Golden oranges tasted delicious and were placed between cups and plates. The brilliance was shining, and they were like bullets now, which are truly precious. The people of the capital did not value them very much at first, but later, because the Concubine Wencheng liked to eat them, the price increased in Tokyo. I lived in Jiangxi and saw that the people of Jizhou were very fond of this fruit. Those who want to keep them for a long time store them in mung beans, which can be kept unchanged for a long time, saying that the nature of mandarin oranges is hot and the nature of beans is cool, so they can last for a long time." Jiangxi golden oranges were regarded as a precious fruit offered to the imperial court during the Northern Song Dynasty. Nowadays, although the ancient meaning of worshiping gold is prevalent, with gold in the first place, golden oranges are not very expensive. Two coppers buy two, and even Shanghai children do not like to eat them. Only the Jinshan honey oranges from the Jin and Yuan dynasties reign supreme for a time. You see, aren't there Huahong honey oranges for sale in Shanghai fruit shops all year round?

Small Toys That Are About to Be Outdated 182

Three Hates 183

— Ouyang Shan

The electric light suddenly went out, and the small shrine was cut off from its breath, swelling from the inside out. The oil lamp on the shrine also seemed to die once, and then slowly come back to life. Someone lit a tallow candle, and a faint, wavering light floated around—the ancient life of centuries ago began around us.

In a quiet, undiscovered corner, a faint dampness emanated. Small cockroaches crept stealthily back and forth in front of my seat. Worker Ahan, young student Fan Zengguang, and his female classmate Chen Qi sat side by side to my right, almost equally spaced. They didn't seem to have moved a muscle.

Hate is a common characteristic of all of us. In ten years, I have never met a purely happy person—there are no such people in China. We breathe in hate, we eat and sleep in it. It occupies as important a position as oxygen. Because Fan Zengguang was determined to make an interesting proposal, it was chosen as a topic for these young people to discuss.

"Okay, you go first."

Ahan said without hesitation,

"Yes, of course, that's the way it is. I hate the kind of person who doesn't have the guts and pretends to be a hero in a place where they shouldn't have the guts... Ask them, they all hate this kind of bastard as much as I do! When it comes to fighting, he's the first to yell, "Bring more, be more aggressive!" He's the first to challenge others, saying, "Got anything to protect? I'll punch you in the chest!" But later... he's the first to get a stomachache!"

Everyone laughed. When it was Chen Qi's turn, she told me in a sharp voice with a burning, stimulating quality,

"My world is small. We don't fight. Therefore, I hate a kind of person who promises you something to your face but doesn't do it afterwards. He never refuses you to your face for something he is determined not to do. There are these hypocritical characters everywhere... I can't forgive him even when I die."

"I also hate a kind of hypocritical character, and I can't forgive him even when I die. But that person is very different from what you're talking about!"

Fan Zengguang shouted excitedly, but then fell silent, looking at everyone in turn before slowly saying:

"This is a short story about love. There was a girl who was very close to me, and we were both very happy. In happiness, we also planned our future in all aspects... But, like all love affairs, she left me for a more glorious goal. At that time, we all liked to call girls "scenery"... Two years later, this scenery came back to me... But I knew her past completely. She had a lover to be proud of. Her lover was a financier who had recently made a fortune from a speculative business.

"I am foolishly devoted, so I still love her the same. Everything is loyal to her. She is a beautiful and charming girl, so she is naturally cunning. She needs my love, but she doesn't need my loyalty—as if that's worthless, ragged cloth. I asked her about something, and she always said she didn't know. She declared that she had never had a lover. "Didn't a certain financier recently make a fortune?" "I have never had a friend who is a speculator in my life." This scenery sees me as a fool! If one day I am escorted to the execution ground to be beheaded, I will still curse her in the red light of blood!..."

While speaking, his long body straightened more and more, as if he wanted to stretch out infinitely, becoming frighteningly thin. Now, like a rubber band, he shrank suddenly and bent to the ground.

Everyone pondered for a while in his narration.

"Now, let's have Uncle Wei tell us."

Someone suggested, but I didn't say anything. Hate is not the same for everyone. In opposite moods—or interests—there are opposite responses. It is meaningless to just point out the hateful aspects of human beings. People do not live to insult others... In fact, I share all three of these hates.

Dead Butterfly 184

— Yi Ping

From what place did it fly,

I can't remember anymore.

A melancholic

Drizzling spring dusk.

How did it die,

I can't remember anymore.

Accompanied by faded green peaches,

And red and blue ink.

Send this miserable corpse to her,

To coax two drops of tears from her:

But she has already stopped crying,

That burning, solid heart.

Seesaw (7) 185

— Zi Chen

Who knew that just stepping out the door, he would run into Little Erzi. Panting anxiously, he yelled at his mother: "Hurry! Hurry! His load was knocked over by someone, and he's fighting with someone. He's going to the police station!"

Mother's hands were shaking uncontrollably. She dropped the two children and said to Little Erzi, "Little Brother Er, please take them back!" Saying that, she ran off. She also dropped the keys.

Little Maotou was about to cry, but Little Erzi coaxed her. Little Monk was a little scared. He saw a group of people fighting across from the reflective wall. Bowls and plates were smashed on the ground. Mother was running there.

Little Erzi led the two children home. Walking under the white powder wall, they still wanted to watch the excitement. They stretched their heads to look, but there was no one on the high frame. The long plank also fell to the ground with one end跷跷板 in the air. They pushed the railing, but it was locked. Little Erzi urged them to go home, and Little Monk took another look at the long plank and the frame underneath it.

Little Erzi went back to sell sugar candy and told them not to go out. Mother was helping Father to fight, and she would be back in a moment.

The two children didn't know what to do. After waiting for a long time, Mother still didn't return. Little Maotou was digging up mud and kneading round balls, trying to make a ball like the ones people kick. But no matter how much she kneaded, it was always too small. Little Monk tried to move a bench against the wall, wanting to climb up and look down. The bench wouldn't stand still, and he couldn't climb up. With a crash, the bench fell over, and Little Maotou's ball was also crushed.

Little Maotou started to cry. Little Monk tried to coax his sister like an adult. His sister ignored him, and he became anxious. He wanted to think of something to make her laugh. Suddenly, he saw the bed where Father slept. The mattress on the bed was lifted, revealing a few long wooden planks. He pulled his sister and ran towards the bed: "Play with that plank!"

Little Maotou rolled her eyes. She also thought of "that plank." How to play with it?

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Widows' Club Organization 186

— Gao Yuan

Fuzhou Correspondence: "Ms. Ding Xiuzhen of Yunxiao County, Fujian, comes from a prominent family. She married young, but unfortunately, before her beauty faded, she lost her husband. The solitary lamp and lonely quilt brought much sorrow. Ms. Ding, being without a husband and finding her empty bed difficult to bear, married a Mr. Overseas Chinese and went to the Philippines. However, the local customs were strict, and they treated her with disdain, subjecting her to cold ridicule and making things difficult for her. Now that her husband has passed away again, Ms. Ding had no choice but to return home. Unexpectedly, the villagers were all ashamed to associate with her. At this point, Ms. Ding felt even more bored. Fortunately, she inherited a substantial estate from her late husband, so she donated 500,000 yuan and gathered like-minded widows to organize a widows' club, giving those who sympathize with each other a place to gather and have fun. It is currently under construction and will be established within September. It will include a theater, dance hall, library, billiard room, and golf course, allowing the widows to express their feelings and avoid other delusions."

This clearly tells us that if one has superior wealth, there are ways to respond to ridicule, although it is not necessarily to organize a widows' club.

Now, this club is about to be established. According to the communication, most of its facilities are for entertainment. Entertainment is a need in life, but it is not life itself. Therefore, using entertainment to eliminate physiological needs is insufficient. It may not be wrong to say that Ms. Ding's facilities are flawed. We must understand that if a person's life is stable, mental pain is greatly reduced. In a society with extreme economic panic, such stability is impossible, especially for women. Under the revivalist wave, some are forced back into the family, while others are ridiculed for remarrying. The establishment of this club is to provide entertainment and comfort to these widows who cannot remarry.

However, with a little thought, we realize that the widows who can participate in entertainment are not the ones without money, but the wealthy ones. Fundamentally, Ms. Ding belongs to the wealthy class, so she naturally will not focus on another group of people. Moreover, the fact that this club includes some widows as like-minded (chaste) only gives powerful support to the revivalist movement, allowing feudal forces to raise their heads higher, which means heavier oppression of women in opposition to feudalism.

Perhaps some will say that the organizers of the club themselves may not think this way, and the above judgment is unjust to them. But we believe that objectively, they are unintentionally or intentionally using entertainment to anesthetize people.

Fallen Leaves 187

— Laoxin

At that time, I was still a child. I remember, clearly remember, in that distant south, a south with many banyan trees, I loved to dream; and I also remember among those many dreams there was one that was not a dream, but reality. —

Alone I walked to the wilderness, a clear and desolate wilderness that had just been washed by a storm. This was a place I was used to, I was very familiar with it, because often when I had no companions, I would throw myself into its embrace, let it comfort my loneliness, let it nurture my weak heart. This time was no exception. After wandering around, I naturally came to the old banyan tree that had accompanied me from the days I began to understand things until then.

The old banyan tree was also very desolate. According to my uncles, it had lived alone for hundreds of years, without any other locust or cypress trees to accompany it, because

Page 18

the soil in this wilderness was originally barren, and planting other vegetable trees or shade trees would not allow them to grow. Therefore, it lived a solitary life for hundreds of years. Perhaps we shared the same feelings, but I always lingered with it. As long as I had a chance, I would accompany it to live my lonely life. From childhood, gloominess covered my eyes. And perhaps this lonely old banyan tree lived an even more terrible life than me—I often heard it crying.

Its crying was very faint, only the small stream that flowed continuously beside it could hear it; and my small building was built beside the stream. Sometimes in the dead of night, the small stream often carried its crying into my ears. When I heard it, my heart was sad. Although I lived alone, I could still find a stable place to sleep at night, but the old and lonely tree only had crying left to prolong its life. At such times, I often thought of going to see it immediately, but even if I strained my eyes at the window, I couldn't see it, because the small stream just made a bend there. On such a night, I would lose sleep, my eyes facing the two huge dots hitting the window, as if hitting my heart, making me feel extremely sad.

The next day, I got up early in the morning, without even wiping my face, and hurriedly walked into the embrace of the wilderness, closer to the pitiful and lonely old banyan tree. I looked at the fallen leaves all over the ground, and I almost couldn't help crying. I picked up a piece of yellowed fallen leaf, held it in my arms, and was about to take it back when suddenly, with a heavy thud, another fallen leaf floated onto my head. Before I could catch it, it floated into the stream.

— Oh, even the tender green leaves are falling?

I stared in horror at the tender green banyan leaf, and my heart became even sadder. I was guessing in my heart, using all my understanding at that time, but I couldn't figure it out. Only the yellowed and old leaves would be torn apart by the storm, how could such a leaf that had not yet grown be eliminated as well? So I came up with many reasons, but I was still not very clear: so I blamed the storm even more. The terrible storm cruelly blew down even this leaf that had not yet grown, allowing its prematurely aged body to live the drifting life of those insulted and harmed.

The rapid current of the stream showed no mercy, it wrapped this tender green fallen leaf in its embrace and sent it all the way downstream. At that time, with a martyr-like sorrowful mood, I followed the stream, all the way sending off the fallen leaf that could not withstand the wind and rain. I watched its tiny body stubbornly struggling in the rapid current, and I was gradually moved. The stream made a bend, and I quickly climbed onto my small building, watching my little companion gradually drift away from me. I raised my hand, silently praying for it, and I no longer cursed the storm, I prayed for its efforts and struggles.

When its shadow also disappeared, I felt that my face was in the wind and rain, I closed the window and collapsed on the bed.

Lucheng Town 188

— You Qi

Just like that, we rested. The time was not early, but not late either. The hands of the clock clearly pointed to six.

Regarding the place where we rested, although it left us with some faint shadows in our impression, we were very vague about its substance. How many families lived in this town, what did it produce, and what position did it occupy in the collapse of the countryside? We had no way of knowing these things. Time determined our journey, and those things required considerable time!

After landing at the inn, the first thing we wanted to know was naturally the name of this town. Therefore, the porters almost became our only opponents in our eyes. What was the result? The opponents disappeared into the other end of the town in the chaotic air. A porter familiar with the path told us that this was Lucheng Town.

If I were to say that I had buried a deep impression in my memory, then Lucheng Town is worth mentioning.

Whether in form or area, it was a cut above the rest. The entrance was a confluence, but when we left, it left two forks. In this V-shaped town road, besides the inns, there were also quite a few small businesses. Perhaps it should be considered a characteristic? In the town, you couldn't see the sky. The roofs on both sides were tightly pressed down by something, not letting in the wind or the sun. Everything was surrounded by darkness, and the people's faces showed a terrible iron-blue color.

The sedan chairs and belongings were supervised and placed on the roof racks specially built in the inn (note). Thus, we walked into the second courtyard.

In front of the second courtyard, there was a large yard. The top of the yard, like the town, did not let in air. Fortunately, there were a few pieces of glass that allowed us to see the color of the sky and the drifting of the clouds. At the same time, we could also see the shape of every corner of this inn.

After taking off the clothes soaked in sweat, "a thorough wash" became a necessary task. We filled the washbasins we brought and the ones the inn had with cool water, occupied them by looting, washed and wiped ourselves, while still grumbling about how hot the weather was today.

In a casual glance, I saw the inn's young waiter leading the teapot up the stairs in the corner, looking very unwilling.

——Ah, there are楼 floors here! I said.

Following these words, our heads couldn't help but raise. Ah, how should I write this? Right at the doorway of the room next to the top of the building, there was a young woman casting a slight glance at us.

Old Huang was probably stunned, not wiping the water from his head, and just stared upwards. The sexual thirst burned the long-dry seedlings in his heart. Maybe he wanted to test his edge? I thought. The woman was very open-minded. Later, she calmly walked down and chatted with Old Huang. Judging from her age, she was in her twenties, but she didn't have a bit of splashy spirit. All she had was some forced pretense.

The afterglow was driven away by the vast night, and the earth gradually fell silent, as if dead outside the town. Dinner was eaten in the light of candles. In order to invigorate our spirits from the day's fatigue, we brought the inn's smoking set, dug out hundreds of coins worth of paste, and puffed out clouds of smoke.

Needless to say, we were all amateurs at smoking. The smoke often burned in our hands, and we couldn't get it to fit properly on the pipe bowl. Frustration and anger welled up in our hearts.

——Let me smoke it for you, the woman smiled, revealing two rows of neat teeth.

Surrounded by these young people in the wooden-framed bamboo beds, we didn't consider the speed of time, nor did we forget the solemnity of the surroundings, and even left tomorrow's itinerary completely behind.

The woman narrated her life story, drifting, stumbling, suffering, fighting against the demonic society with her lonely body. Finally, she cried, and crystal tears hung in her eyes. She asked Old Huang to sympathize with her unfortunate life, at least to hope that he could give some assistance in material terms. Of course, the so-called assistance was not empty. She hoped to exchange her body for the above price.

Old Huang's intention wavered a little, but he didn't reply immediately. The mountain wind brought the snores of the servants, telling us that it was already late. Because of the inherent instincts of friendship, I hinted to him with my eyes——

——Be careful, this harmful woman!

Finally, Old Huang resolutely let her go. Holding a belly full of anger, she resentfully resented the person who destroyed the good deed, and walked out in a huff, disappearing into the dim light.

Note: Roof racks, racks installed on the roof to prepare for placing things like sedan chairs.

Rural Miscellany 189

— Ai Tu

The days passed as long and slow as the crawling of ants. In the countryside, no one will deny that this is an extremely depressing thing. When I drifted across the vast sea and returned to the embrace of my hometown, everything I felt was painful. Although I quietly returned to my village and saw my haggard, pale-faced, pitiful mother, her sickly, weak body always caused me pain. When the aunt next door ran over to see me, she quietly told me:

"Her body is getting worse. Look at her face! Not long ago, she fell ill, which was really scary. You've been wandering and haven't come home for two years. Now you should comfort her!"

Too unintentional! My heart felt as if it was being twisted. I was very ashamed, but what could I do? Heaven knows my pain. On the harsh journey, wasn't I always inseparable from the circle of pain? Now I have returned with my body covered in wounds. Seeing such an ugly mother, my heart was even more soaked in a bitter alcohol, gradually swelling like fire and burning. But at this time, I stirred up another thought, like a roar, like resentment, like tragedy. I will never forget the extremely selfish, gossipy, and mean aspects of the women in the countryside. For example, no one was ever willing to help my mother, but there were many people who gossiped about her behind her back. In short, the women in the countryside are all the same: people without thoughts. At the same time, I thought of my brother. Didn't he marry a woman for the sake of our mother? Why did he abandon our poor mother and take his wife to another place? Thinking about the painful breath, I tightly covered myself.

After returning home, I learned that my uncle, who had been in the United States for more than ten years, had returned. But when I talked to him, he seemed afraid that I would borrow money from him. Before long, he made an excuse to leave me. What a ridiculous and stingy person! Yes, these people occupy a large part of the countryside. I hated it and left my poor hometown unhappy. Leaving my poor mother again, like a person without a home, I quietly embarked on the journey.

But the countryside is indeed annoying. Before I even left my hometown, many local gentrymen talked to me about lawsuits in the countryside, such as the prohibition of opium and private sales! Assaults! Adultery! Many things had to be discussed with me. They all regarded me as a young gentleman who had returned from the city. But in my heart, this was all just annoying, just a despicable trick for the local tyrants and evil gentry to attack each other.

Leaving my poor hometown, I wandered for a long time in the clean and complicated county town. Everything I felt was empty. Besides the party's arrogance and the intense breath that occupied the breath of all the people, everything was just the charming but false big discount signs! Following the wind blowing from the southern sea, the bodies of the pretentious women swayed on the smooth cement roads under the white sun. Everything was no different from the metropolis, except that the place was so small that it was enough to make people feel bored in less than two hours.

In the evening, I took a rapid train to a friend's house in a village in the north of the countryside.

This place was very quiet, almost like being deep in the mountains. In less than two days, I felt the fatigue of silence and the extreme boredom of rural life. Apart from two or three children coming to play on the building, it was almost so calm and desolate.

At night, the countryside was already drunk in a circle of calmness and darkness. The high sky was as black as a vast piece of charcoal, and the small stars were flashing. At this time, there was no sound of dogs barking, no human voices. This was absolutely different from the sleepless city, how terrible! But sometimes there were exceptions, encountering two or three foul-mouthed women cursing each other in hatred. When the constant curses, unpleasant words, and loud noises filled the night space, I hated them for deliberately disturbing people's peaceful dreams. I felt very annoyed. In short, I felt that the uneducated women in the countryside were the most terrible.

Because of all the unfamiliarity, I couldn't help but quickly leave my poor hometown and quietly embark on the journey again, drifting to wander.

Therefore, the two words "modernity" are arsenic poison. It is necessary to be very careful with comparing freedom. I hope everyone doesn't go too far with modernity.

If you can only play a certain type of role that matches your own personality well, then the scope is too narrow. Shenbao Architectural Weekly

The Meaning of Modern Architectural Beauty (Part 1) 201

— By Taniguchi Yoshiro, Translated by Zhang Guangzheng

(1)

The appearance of so-called modern architecture can be excessively perceived as dry and tasteless. The richness of emotion is lost in the dull appearance, affecting people's feelings of unease about social life. Such criticisms are often heard.

But before making such criticisms, we must deeply explore the so-called "new architecture" of contemporary architectural masterpieces. Facing the simple posture and pure, unadorned nature of modern architecture, one inevitably wonders where the architect's painstaking efforts were spent. And there are quite a few people who think that it is simply a crude work that is very easy to design.

This is because in the past, many exaggerated, ornate adjectives and words of admiration for its exquisite skills were used to describe famous buildings. Therefore, the general public believes that without decoration, it is not a beautiful building, and without skills, it is not a famous building. Consequently, the beauty of architecture in the eyes of the general public is seen as the dazzling carvings and colors of the Nikko Tosho-gu in Japan, or the large scale of St. Peter's Basilica in Rome. At the very least, one demands the extremely intricate marble decorations, such as the dense Saracenis temple. However, in modern architecture, one also demands high, old-fashioned spires like medieval temples, or the lavish construction of palace-style railings; using these as standards of architectural beauty, modern architecture, which lacks decorative variation, is judged as non-artistic. This view is not without exaggeration.

(2)

But the architecture that new architects expect is not that kind of decorative architecture that embellishes the exterior with skills. On the contrary, they put the exterior into question. On this point, a fundamental difference arises with the general public's study of architectural beauty.

The starting point of modern architecture is based on "application". The architect's painstaking design is to seek how to technically solve this "application" problem. How to meet the internal requirements, and use this point as a factor in forming the external appearance. Therefore, the external appearance is only an expression of internal requirements.

For example, due to the necessity of light entering, the size and direction of the windows are determined by the relationship between the direction and part of the sunlight shining; in addition, opening ornate windows on the front to show off the appearance is not necessary. At the same time, due to the need for ventilation, technical attention is given to all the details of the structure of the windows, the method of opening, etc.; in addition, the technique of decorating the curve pattern of the windows becomes an unnecessary object that hinders light from entering and obstructs ventilation. The main entrance is located with the aim of convenient access; in addition, building it in the central part of the front to ignore the inconvenience of the location for the sake of the appearance of the grand hall is simply a violation of the fundamental spirit of architecture in modern architecture. According to the consideration of internal traffic, the configuration of each room is determined by the connection and its efficiency, so there is no need to insist on left-right symmetry on the appearance without being bound by the previous forms.

Today's architects hold this attitude: Only in the construction of government offices and other buildings, the so-called left-right symmetry can produce a solemn and majestic idea on the appearance, and the design conditions that are necessary for left-right symmetry are incorporated. Therefore, even in cases where the location of the site is disadvantageous, a large gate in the center of the front is still set up. The method of extending the two wings to the left and right is adopted, and the functional inconvenience that occurs inside is risked. That is, the method of determining the combination of the interior by the exterior. That, of course, requires artistic architects to handle. At the same time, it can also be said that in order to embellish the exterior, the interior is made to obey.

The claim of modern architecture is the opposite. Solving the interior is the fundamental problem, and the exterior is only an accessory; few people believe that the function of the building will still be expressed on the exterior. Consequently, we deeply know that the previous buildings were actually deformed buildings, violating the original meaning of architecture. So, they have collectively advocated that the necessary functional extreme expression of the building is the true posture of the building, and the true beauty of the building. The external engineering materials that are directly presented to the vision are aimed at maintaining durability in weathering. Inside, materials with heat resistance are sought to prevent the transmission of heat.

Analysis of the Interior of Ancient Chinese Architecture (Part 1) 202

— Zhiyun

The construction industry in China has had considerable development from the 19th century until now, but compared with European and American countries, it is far behind. In this foreign concession of Shanghai, although there are also Chinese-built high-rise buildings of more than 20 stories, all the interior decorations are mostly imported, and the annual imports are quite considerable when calculated.

All the buildings in the mainland, whether they are palaces, halls, temples, or civilian houses, all the interior and exterior decorations can be said to be self-sufficient, and in terms of the firmness of construction, they are not inferior to all Westernized buildings.

Here, let's briefly talk about all the interior decorations of old Chinese buildings:

(1) Design - The architecture of Chinese temples is similar in form to that of India, encompassing layers of courtyards, corridors, kitchens, dining rooms, and monks' dormitories. The formal form is three solemn, single-story halls with parallel exposed wooden roofs, attached to wide staircases, arches, and bridges. Residences are similar to temples and face south. Outside the front door is a large courtyard with houses on both sides. At the other end is a large hall, followed by another courtyard; sometimes there is a third courtyard, which is prepared for women. Behind it is a garden. All the windows are mostly open to the inside.

The "threshold" outside the door also has a certain proportion in its construction. Its height is determined according to the height of the eaves from the ground: one foot and one inch, that is, the eaves are one foot from the ground. If the threshold is one inch high, the eaves are two feet from the ground, then the height of the threshold is two inches, and so on.

Concrete Ships (Part 2) 203

— Xu Pusheng

Now, let us put aside the historical description of the shipbuilding plans of various countries and briefly mention the advantages of concrete ships. They are stable and do not roll easily when sailing, do not leak water under normal conditions, are easy to repair in the event of a collision, and are difficult to burn even if they catch fire, all of which are its notable features.

Comparing this with steel ships, in terms of cost, concrete ships are on average only 60% to 80% of the cost of full-steel ships of the same load. If the two have equal deadweight tonnage, the hull of the concrete ship is larger, so it will be more efficient than steel ships when transporting bulky cargo.

There are three ways to build a concrete ship. Now, let's pick up Feng Xiong's book "Sanhetu" and summarize the main points of the method of building this type of ship for introduction:

(1) Integral Construction Method The entire ship is integrated, and the situation is the same as the construction of concrete structures on land. The bottom of the slipway is arranged with concrete bricks, and the entire hull is formed with plate molds. First, arrange the outer plate molds to determine the outer shape of the hull. Place steel bars inside this plate mold as the skeleton. The transverse frame and longitudinal stringer are framed and placed in plate molds according to their shapes. The bulkhead, decking, hatchway coaming, etc. are all built when the hull is about to be completed, and the method is the same.

(2) Separate Construction Method This method is quite common in the UK. According to the shape of the hull, it is divided into multiple grids. The grid frame is made as a whole and made of concrete, and the grid plates are separately made and embedded in it. However, there are also those who only make the main grid frame as a whole, and the remaining grid frames are all separately made and embedded, which is the same as making grid plates.

(3) Bone Construction Method First, use steel bars to form the skeleton of the hull, and plaster the inner and outer surfaces with high-quality concrete. (This is the method used by Lambot for the first concrete ship, which was popular in Italy). There are also those who adopt this method and add changes, that is, use steel bars to form a double-layer hull, fill it with concrete in the middle, and then plaster the inner and outer surfaces with concrete, which is especially strong.

Comparing the above three methods, each has its advantages and disadvantages. If used properly, good results can be achieved. Which method to choose should be determined by the size of the ship and its use; roughly, large ships for sea voyages should use the integral construction method, while those for inland river navigation are suitable for the bone construction method.

Since concrete, an artificial stone material, can be made into ships that sail on the vast ocean, if future research is deeper and the techniques are improved, it may not be absolutely impossible to make it into an airplane to conquer the sky.
